##### 4.2.2.5.7 Combined Wake Events
- Certain wake events are combined outside of the masking supported though
WAKE_AOWAKE_MASK_W register in the wake engine. Specific cases are as follows:
- Wake events from AO mail boxes: Four mail boxes supported in SPE cluster can generate
individual wake events. These events are merged with the SPE_AUTO_WAKE (i.e., wake event from SPE due to outgoing transactions in SC7) to drive a specific SPE wake input to the
- WAKE engine. There are individual wake mask bits supported for the combined (OR ’Ed) mail
box wake event, and SPE_AUTO_WAKE. SPE_AUTO_WAKE is defeatured due to certain limitations in the AXI Blocking logic.
- AO debug wake: AO debug wake is an OR ‘ed version of iLA wake and SPE WDT expiry fourth
expiry.
- Xusb2wake_event 2: Due to limited number of wake events supported in hardware, wake 78
is OR-ed version of fourth wake event from XUSB (i.e., xusb2wake_event_3) and xusb2wake_event_2.

- PMC Functional Description
##### 4.2.2.5.8 Power Gate Control Sequencer
The following state diagram captures the high-level sequences executed by the PMC Power Gate Sequencer. The inputs triggering the PG Sequencer are: 1.
- Reset logic asserting reset_sd_remove_req. This is a specific request to PG sequencer to
remove shutdown controls when the L0/L1/L2 cold reset is de-asserted. A software power control request coming through a power domain-specific PMC_POWER_GATE_CONTROL register.
- Request from SC7 FSM (sc7_assert/remove_sd_req) to assert the shutdown controls for the
SRAMs in the VDD_CORE domain.
- Retention request from AOPM (pm2pmc_ret_Req). This is a request from the AOPM to put all
the AOPG RAMs in retention mode.
- Logic Power gating request from the AOPG hardware state machine in the PMC. The request
to the AOPG hardware FSM is sent by the AOPM Deep dormant state machine. 2. 3. 4. 5.
**Figure 4.28 Power Gating Sequencer**
The preceding figure is a generic state diagram that depicts all the possible transitions between logic and RAM power gating modes.
##### 4.2.2.5.9 Power Gated Partitions
- The following is a summary and general guideline of power controls leaving PMC. Power Gate
control FSM in PMC drives these controls through Software/Hardware hooks specified in earlier sections. 1.
- LOGIC_SLEEP Mode
- PMC provides LOGIC_SLEEP controls for all SoC, CV, DVD-D, and AON power domains of PG
type.

- PMC Functional Description
2.
- SRAM_SLEEP Mode
- PMC provides these controls for all SRAMs in the SoC, CV, DVD-D, and AON partitions. This
includes all types of PG domains. Note CVSRAM (FCM based, in CVNAS) controls are not driven from PMC.
- SRAM_RET Mode
- RET mode is supported only for RAMs in AO-PG and AO-NPG power domains that are sourced
from PMC. 3.
##### 4.2.2.5.10 SRAM Control from PMC
The preceding controls are sequenced along with the partition logic power-gating controls. This section captures the specific approach supported in PMC to accomplish efficient power control of the partitions, with minimal wire usage.
##### 4.2.2.5.11 SRAM and Logic Power Mode Matrix
From a partition power-controlling perspective, there are three basic modes that are supported in the PMC so that the logic and SRAMs in a partition can be sequenced to the most desirable power state. These modes are:
- SRAM retention mode
- SRAM sleep mode
- Logic sleep mode
The table below captures the allowed power states for SRAM and logic in a partition.
- Logic Sleep
- SRAM Sleep
- SRAM Retention
- Notes
- None
- RAM Retention
- RAM Sleep
- Retention is don't care
- ILLEGAL
- RET+ LOGIC_SLEEP
- RAM SLEEP+ LOGIC SLEEP
- RAM SLEEP+ LOGIC SLEEP
All the allowed states for logic and SRAM can be entered by appropriately configuring the control registers in the PMC. If software makes an illegal request (where the logic power down is requested and SRAMs are not in low-power mode), the power gating hardware defaults this request to LOGIC_SLEEP = 1, SRAM_SLEEP = 1 case, and update the status register accordingly.

- PMC Functional Description
- Software checks the PMC_IMPL_<PART>_POWER_GATE_STATUS register to confirm the success of
the power gating request.
##### 4.2.2.5.12 AON Module Power Control
AON cluster contains SRAMs and power gated logic, similar to SoC partitions. However, there are subtle differences in the way power control is handled for these modules.
- AON SRAM Control
The following is the list of SRAMs supported in the power gated part of the AON cluster (AOPG). The PMC drives the individual SLEEP/RET controls for each of these SRAMs:
- L1 I and D-cache
- BTCM0 and BTCM1 bank 0
- BTCM0 and BTCM1 bank 1
- BTCM0 and BTCM1 bank 2
- BTCM0 and BTCM1 bank 3
- BTCM0 and BTCM1 bank 4
- BTCM0 and BTCM1 bank 5
- BTCM0 and BTCM1 bank 6
- BTCM0 and BTCM1 bank 7
- CAN message RAM 0
- CAN message RAM 1
- Like the SoC SRAM controls, the the AO SRAM controls' default is to bring them up in the
functional mode at boot time. Once the system is active, the only way to put these RAMs in SLEEP mode, is through software hooks in the respective POWER_GATE_CONTROL register. SC7 transitions in hardware do not assert these controls for the AO SRAMs. In addition to the software hooks to put the AOPG RAMs in retention mode, the AOPM hardware implements a handshake with the PMC during AON low-power state transitions. The AONPG domain contains the MSS AO encryption RAM, the MSS scratch SRAM, and the PMC scratch SRAM. For these SRAMs, the PMC exposes all the SRAM control hooks (i.e., SRAM_SLEEP, SRAM_RET) to software. On receiving this request, the PMC PG controller starts sequencing the RAMs one after the other. Once the final RAM is put in the intended state, it sends an ack back to the AOPM.
- AON Logic PG Control
- The AON cluster supports one power gated domain. The AOPM makes use of the PMC power
gating sequencer to assert logic sleep controls to this power gated domain. The AOPM requests the PMC to control power through a dedicated hardware interface.

- PMC Functional Description
- PMC_IMPL_AO_PG_TIMERS register specifies the delay between the sleep and clamp signals for
AON logic. This power gating request to PMC occurs only when committed to is treated as one power domain (AONPG). A single clamp signal (hardware controlled) is driven by the PMC to the AO cluster to handle the isolation of power gated modules. Before the AOPM requests logic power gating to the PMC, the AO SRAMs are put in a low-power mode (SRAM Retention) through the AOPM RAM retention request, so that illegal SRAM scenarios are prevented.
#### 4.2.2.6 Pad Controls
The PMC sources the DPD controls for the MPIOs and I/O bricks in the system. There are two ways the pads are put into DPD mode. 1. 2.
- When the respective control bit is set by the software in IO_DPD_REQ register
- When SC7 mode is entered SC7 FSM ensures that all pads (except the DDR pads) are put into
DPD mode unless the DPD mode entry is specifically masked.
##### 4.2.2.6.1 Latching Support in the Pads
In the current pad designs, EN/A/E_PULLU/E_PULLD gets captured at the rising edge of SEL_DPD signal.
##### 4.2.2.6.2 DPD Control Details
1.
- PMC drives I/O rail-specific SEL_DPD signals. These signals are the primary source of the
latching control in the pads from a software point of view. IO_DPD_REQ register updates drive E_DPD and SEL_DPD in the required sequence.
- SEL_DPD signals driven by the DPD FSM in the PMC are OR’d with the DPD FSM driven
signals to drive the final set of signals seen by the pads (ensuring no illegal state of the pads (SEL_DPD = 0, E_DPD =1), even if the software does not exercise the IO_DPD_REQ controls.
- IO_DPD_OFF_MASK registers (PMC_IMPL_IO_DPD7_OFF_MASK and
- PMC_IMPL_IO_DPD8_OFF_MASK) are used to prevent entry into DPD mode of selected I/Os
in the AON domain. When the MASK bit is set the respective I/O is prevented from entering the DPD mode by a hardware request (from the SC7 FSM). The reset defaults of these registers are to mask the DPD entry for AO I/Os. 2. 3. The SEL_DPD controls are used to hold a pad in a fixed state until software has taken specific actions to reestablish the desired pin state from the pad driver point of view. Software can set multiple IO_DPD_REQ registers bits at the same time, indicating a request to put multiple I/Os into DPD. The CODE field of IO_DPD_REQ register indicates whether the transition is into or out of DPD modes. The PMC supports separate DPD sequencing logic for each IO_DPD_REQ register. There are eight such instances in the PMC. The PMC DPD sequencing logic services each set of controls concurrently until all pending requests are complete. Once a set of DPD sequencing is complete the respective bit is updated in the IO_DPD_STATUS register.

- PMC Functional Description
All the software driven XUSB pad controls and the corresponding registers are moved to XUSBAO. Only the global override from the SC7 FSM is driven to these pads from the PMC.
##### 4.2.2.6.3 PWR_DET Controls
PWR_DET controls are used to indicate if a pad is powered by 3.3V, 1.8V, or 1.2V.
- The detection mechanism has been removed from the pads and replaced by software configured
registers (at reset, these registers indicate that the pad is powered by the higher of the supported power supply options as this is the electrically safe setting). E_18V_PWR – This register content specifies if the respective I/O rail is powered by 1.2V (when the respective register bit is 0) or 1.8V (when the respective register bit is 1). E_33V_PWR – This register content specifies if the respective I/O rail is powered by 1.8V (when the respective register bit is 0) or 3.3V (when the respective register bit is 1).
#### 4.2.2.7 Voltage Monitoring Support
- PMC supports hooks to monitor VDD_CORE, VDD_CPU0/1 rail voltages, OSC, and 32 kHz clock
frequencies. Voltage monitoring is a power security feature where the voltage levels of specific rails are monitored and checked for following potential voltage violations:
- Under/over voltages with respect to the thresholds
- Glitches/Spikes
The following rails require voltage monitoring support. They are supported through the AVFS and PMC modules.
- VDD_CPU0/1
- VDD_CORE
For the AVFS core domains, a digital comparator is added in the CAR modules to check the ADC output against the preconfigured minimum and maximum threshold level and it outputs the voltage fault information. These faults are routed to PMC, which provides configuration registers to select the fault action (Reset/Interrupt) on any voltage violation. Each of the fault actions can be individually enabled.
#### 4.2.2.8 Clock Monitoring
##### 4.2.2.8.1 Safety Requirement for Clock Monitoring
- In automotive platforms, this SoC (when it is deemed safe by an external safety MCU) has a
mechanism where the critical clocks are constantly monitored for:

- PMC Functional Description
- DC faults
Frequency outside of expected ranges.
- Clock Monitoring Features
This frequency monitoring logic in the PMC is used to monitor the OSC and the 32 kHz clocks to detect the following violations: 1. 2. Clock is turned off (DC faults) while monitoring is enabled. Clock frequency is outside of programmed limits. Monitoring logic supports programmable options to generate an interrupt and/or reset and/or fault to the HSM on violations. Each of these resultant actions can be individually enabled.
##### 4.2.2.8.2 RO-Based Clock Monitoring
The mechanism to support OSC clock monitoring is based on an on-die oscillator, which provides the time base to check whether XTAL (or more commonly referred to as OSC) frequency is within expected limits. A module called VRefRO with higher accuracy level sources this clock.
#### 4.2.2.9 FSI Rail Clamp
PMC provides a clamp enable control for clamping the signals originating from FSI to AON and SoC domains. This clamp enable control is implemented on L2 cold reset. Asserted by reset default. De-asserted in hardware based on FSI enabling fuses.
- Fuse-based trigger is fsi_ram_repair_enable_OSC_sync || (fuse_valid_OSC_sync_staged &&
~opt_fsi_disable_OSC_sync).
- Opt_fsi_disable is the Floor sweeping fuse control. This FS fuse value does not take
effect until fuse sensing is done.
- For RAM repair operation, fsi clamp must be de-asserted. Whether RAM repair for FSI is
enabled or not is decided based on fsi_ram_repair_enable fuse. - - Note that this clamp is not software controllable. Like the DVD-D clamp, this clamp enable control also has test overrides i.e., jtag, bscan mode as mentioned in section Boundary Scan Override. To support SC7 with FSI OFF, FSI clamps will also be asserted during SC7 entry and de-assert on the SC7 exit i.e., the assertion/deassertion is controlled by the SC7 sequencer driven pmc2main_clamp.
- Note that FSI clamp does not have an early version for clock gating. There are no clock
crossings originating from FSI.

- PMC Functional Description
- Also, the pmc2main_clamp version used for FSI clamp toggling, does not have any DFD
overrides that bypass the assertion during SC7 debug modes.
#### 4.2.2.10 AO Power State
Multiple versions of the SC7 state are supported in PMC. As mentioned in the interface with AOPM for PG section, this is based on the level of power gating and/or clock gating supported in SPE cluster. The PMC interfaces to the AO PM (Always on Power Management module) to enforce the appropriate SC7-AON power state. The PMC holds off the power gating of AON logic unless SC7 entry is committed.
#### 4.2.2.11 CV Power State
##### 4.2.2.11.1 Default State of CV Logic and RAM Power Gating Controls
The default reset state of the CV logic power controls comes up power-gated on cold boot.
- Software power u-gates them using the partition-specific POWER_GATE_CONTROL register. The
default reset state of the RAM power controls is in SLEEP mode on cold boot. Software brings them out of SLEEP mode using the partition-specific POWER_GATE_CONTROL register post logic power ungating actions. During SC7, the PMC SC7 state machine does not control the RAM/logic states. Software brings the RAM and Logic up, once CV rail is powered up. The PMC does not drive any of the RAM power controls for CV-SRAM (FCM based). The local SRAM controller in the CV domain drives those controls.
##### 4.2.2.11.2 CV Clamp Control
- PMC supports the PMC_IMPL_CV_RG_CNTRL_0_CLAMP register in the PMC_IMPL page for CV rail
isolation. The reset default of this clamp asserts and clamps the interface. This control uses L2 cold reset
#### 4.2.2.12 CCPLEX Power State
PMC does not maintain the power/rail gate status indication for CPUs. There is no PMC involvement in controlling the CCPLEX-SRAM states.
#### 4.2.2.13 GPU SRAM Control
- PMC drives the rail-gating clamp control to the GPU. The controls clamp the GPU->SoC
crossings.PMC_IMPL_GPU_RG_CNTRL_0_RAIL_CLAMP is asserted by default. Boot software unclamps the interfaces once the GPU is powered up. This clamp is also on L2 cold reset. With the

- PMC Functional Description
merged SRAM rail in the iGPU, GVDD_POWERGODD is no longer needed. This is tied off in PMC. Also, the SD_ENTRY_DONE and SD_EXIT_DONE are no longer needed in PMC.
#### 4.2.2.14 SRAM Controls
The 16FF-LR single rail NV compiler RAMs support the following power-saving options:
- Sleep mode: Reduces leakage by power gating both the periphery and the bit cell array. The
context is lost. Retention mode: Peripheral logic is power-gated while the bit cell array is left powered on.
- Table 4.20 SRAM Power Control Matrix
- SRAM power
controls
- SLEEP Mode
- Retention Mode
- Functional Mode
- Usage
- SLEEP_EN [7:0]
8xFF 8xFF 8x00
- Used to control the RAM power-
gaters.
- RET_EN
- Used for enabling retention
mode.
##### 4.2.2.14.1 RAM Dump
PMC supports a hardware mechanism to flush the CPU Caches and put the DRAM in self-refresh, so that hard hang scenarios can be debugged. A part of the RAMDUMP FSM is in MSS_AON. The PMC RAMDUMP FSM requests MSS_AON to put DDR bricks in the DPD and the DRAM in self-refresh. MSS_AO acknowledges to the PMC, once the requested actions are complete. Since the HSM can request for L2 cold reset, RAM Dump can be enabled on both the WDT and HSM triggered L2 cold resets using PMC_IMPL_RAMDUMP_CTL_STATUS_0[RAMDUMP_EN] setting.
- Both Cache flush request and DRAM self-refresh request from PMC are qualified with
RAMDUMP_EN control in order to avoid single point failure cases and to reduce the failure rate.
#### 4.2.2.15 Power-on-Detector (POD)
Power-on-detector cells are deployed for various core rails in the chip. This cell detects the power off to on event of the power rail it is powered by and take the following actions: Request for a L0 system-wide reset. This request is also sent to CAR to trigger a reset for the respective rail domain. Send a fault indication to HSM ( using Error Collator). Send an indication to PSC for its turtle mode.

- PMC Functional Description
The configuration registers corresponding to all the PODs are placed in PMC_IMPL page. At a high level,
- PMC implements a reset masking control per rail domain with POD. All the Reset masking
registers in PMC are protected under a single SCR. They are routed to the CAR logic in respective rail domains for generation of domain-specific resets.
- PMC also implement a POD_GLOBAL_MONITOR register, which contains the status of error
indications from the frontend and backend logic inside POD.
- Note that there is a second set of monitoring trigger registers that are present in the
respective rail domains. In PMC, the monitoring trigger register for VDD_RTC POD is implemented.
- For pre-IST software to mask the reset request from PODs, a sample and hold JTAG logic is
implemented. This is required for IST operation, where software will program the POD bypass software register and IST software will sample-and-hold the value. The reset enable controls are set to ENABLE state once the system enters SC7 state. (i.e., once SoC rail is powered down. The SC7 sequencer state indicating clamp assertion is used for updating these registers in HW. Global monitoring registers are reset by the signal whose status is logged in the register. Local monitoring registers for VRTC_POD can be on L2 cold reset. The raw reset request (the signal that is not qualified by the reset enable control) from each POD is routed as a fault to the HSM through AON Error collator and to PSC for turtle mode.
#### 4.2.2.16 Security Canary Path Monitor (SCPM)
To detect the glitches on the critical clock and voltage rail domains, SCPMs are deployed in the chip. This module triggers a reset request if clock runs fast enough to break a timing path modeled in SCPM or when a glitch occurs. L0 async reset is generated out of the reset request from SCPM. In PMC, SCPM is instanced to detect glitches on the OSC clock in VDD_RTC domain. This instance will be referred to as AON_XTAL_SCPM. In addition to the AON_XTAL_SCPM and its registers, PMC houses registers for the SOC_XTAL_SCPM, which will be placed near fuse controller block in SoC.
- This is to ensure that its configuration settings are retained across SC7 and that the
- SOC_XTAL_SCPM can immediately start functioning once warm reset is de-asserted during SC7
exit.
- In addition to AON_XTAL_SCPM’s ERROR_OUT generated within PMC, it also receives ERROR OUT
indications from SOC_XTAL_SCPM, BPMP_R5_SCPM, consolidated indication from FSI SCPMs and PSC_SE_SCPM for L0 async reset generation. This ERROR_OUT that is received by PMC is the error signal qualified with IOEnable and DFTEnable. This input is further qualified with RESET_EN config bit (PMC_IMPL_SCPM_RESET_EN register(with a separate SCR)) before using it in system reset generation logic.

- PMC Functional Description
During SC7 entry, AON_XTAL_SCPM input clock is gated using the osc_stable indication from SC7
- HW sequencer. The SCPM clock comes up once osc_stable goes high during SC7 exit. The reset
enable controls are set to ENABLE state once the system enters SC7 state. (i.e once SoC rail is powered down. The SC7 sequencer state indicating early clamp assertion is used for updating these registers in hardware.
#### 4.2.2.17 Storage Space
##### 4.2.2.17.1 PMC Scratch Registers
PMC supports always-on storage in the form of secure and non-secure scratch registers. This SRAM module supports its own power control knobs through a PMC register. This entire scratch SRAM is in RET in the SC state. In addition to SRAM-based scratch, PMC also supports flop-based scratch registers: (PMC_SCRATCH_0_0 and PMC_SCRATCH_0_1). These are specifically used for storing software flags used in SC7 flow.
- SECURE_SCRATCH4-7: Reserved
- SECURE_SCRATCH8-15: Reserved
- SECURE_SCRATCH16-23: These enable VDD_RTC rail monitoring, 256 bits i.e., eight 32K flop-
based registers are added in PMC. PMC supports a 384 x 32-sized scratch RAM. In addition, in order to enable half-word parity, the scratch size is no w 384 x 34 bits.

#### 4.2.2.18 LED Blink and Breathing
The PMC provides the control for blinking LED in runtime and SC7 usage. The blinking control is a
- PWM signal. To generate a PWM signal, the PMC has a counter with two programmable values
indicating the ON and OFF periods (in multiple of 16 cycles of the 32.768 kHz clock). The counter is 16 bits long, for a maximum ON period of 215 * 16 / 32.768 103 or about 16 seconds and OFF period of 216 * 16 / 32.768 103 or about 32 seconds.
**Figure 4.29 LED Blink Functionality**
##### 4.2.2.18.1 Muxed Blink and Breathing (Soft Blink)
LED Breathing functionality is multiplexed onto the BLINK outputs as shown in the following figure. LED Breathing controller basically tunes the LED such that it slowly ramps up and ramps down.

- PMC Programming Guidelines
“Blink_en” is used to select between blink and Led breathing (Soft blink) as shown in the table below. If both “Blink_en” and “Led_breathing_en” are set, then blink functionality gets the priority.
**Figure 4.30 Muxed Blink Scheme**
### 4.2.3 PMC Programming Guidelines
#### 4.2.3.1 SC7 Hardware Sequencer
This entire sequencer is in 32 kHz clock domain. The hardware sequencer is triggered when the
- BPMP software writes the DPD_ENABLE register after specifying the target power state
[PMC_IMPL_SC7_CONFIG_0_SC7_TARGET= SC7].
- The BPMP software excludes the AO I/Os used in SC7 state by setting up the
- PMC_IMPL_IO_SYS_DPD_OFF_MASK_0, PMC_IMPL_IO_AO_HV_DPD_OFF_MASK_0 and
- PMC_IMPL_IO_AO_DPD_OFF_MASK_0 registers before triggering hardware actions. This way the
required pads for SPE operation while in SC7 they are excluded from entering DPD.

- PMC Programming Guidelines
**Figure 4.31 SC7 Hardware Sequencer**
The first state in the sequencer i.e., SC7_ASSERT_SLEEP exists in hardware but is not exercised/ tied off as all partitions' power gating actions are triggered on L2 warm reset assertion. Similarly, the SC7_REMOVE_SLEEP state is also not used. Pmc2car_ram_awake signal still goes LOW during entry and de-asserted on exit to keep the reset sequencing.

- PMC Programming Guidelines
- The hardware sequencer asserts the global SEL_DPD and after a programmable delay (in 32K
cycles), the global E_DPD is asserted. These global signals do not override the DDR pad controls. On the SC7 exit, once VDD_CORE is powered ON, the global E_DPD is de-asserted, and on expiry of the DPD timer, global SEL_DPD is de-asserted. The hardware sequencer proceeds through
- SC7_EARLY/MAIN_CLAMP, SC7_PWR_OFF states to enter SC7_ALLOW_AOPG state. A delay step
(RESIDENCY_THRESHOLD_CHECK) is implemented before entering SC7_ALLOW_AOPG state, so that potential “thrashing” of power gate/un-gate actions can be avoided for AO domain. Once in
- SC7_ALLOW_AOPG state, AOPM gets the indication (in the form of ao_pmc2pm_soc_wake_req = 0)
that AO power gating can be triggered.
- Once SC7 sequencer is in ALLOW_AOPG state, AOPM can request a power down of AO logic. When
such a request is seen by the PMC, the PG sequencer triggers AOPG actions. The AOPG sequencer (inside the PG controller module) will indicate the completion of power-gating actions to AOPM by asserting an ack. PMC is required to always respond to a power gating request with an ack.
- SC7_ALLOW_AOPG or SC7_OSC_OFF can be the destination state for SC7 transitions, depending
on whether shallow/deep dormant states are entered in AOPM. The SC7 exit is triggered when a valid wake (Tier 1 or Tier 2) is detected by the Wake engine. AOPM requests the PMC sequencer to reenable OSC and power ungates the AO domain as required (if the wake events meant for SPE cluster are triggered).
- The PMC sequencer prioritizes wake events over a request to power off OSC, if they happen
at the same time. SC7 reset (all warm resets i.e., l*warm reset) seen by VDD_CORE domain is asserted by the SC7 sequencer prior to entering the PWR_ON state. The SC7 reset deassertion occurs in the REMOVE_RESET state, which is entered only after making sure that the ack is seen by the PMC and after all other actions (i.e., clamp deassertion, DPD, and SD removal) are completed. This check guarantees that the PMC never takes the SoC logic out of reset before ensuring that all power- saving steps taken by AOPM and PMC while in SC7 they are completely reversed and the transition back to active state is permitted. Two to three 32 kHz clock cycles before the SC7 reset assertion, the clock stop indication is asserted then de-asserted one 32 kHz post-SC7 reset assertion. This signal is used as an indication by AOCAR module to gate the clocks active during SC7 reset assertion during debug mode, to avoid glitches on the clocks, which are used by debug related modules in SoC.
- There is a PMC_IMPL_SC7_DEBUG_CTRL_0_GLITCH_FREE_CLKEN bit provided to enable/disable
assertion of this clock stop indication control. In functional SC7 mode, this bit should be set to 0, which implies legacy mode. In SC7 debug mode, this bit should be set to 1, when warm_rst_debug override is not set.

- PMC Programming Guidelines
- The SC7 sequencer does not support ASSERT_SLEEP and REMOVE_SLEEP states. On warm
reset assertion, all RAM and logic SLEEP control corresponding to SoC Partitions (except XUSB partitions) are forced to asserted state.
##### 4.2.3.1.1 Programming the OSC Pad Controls
The OSC pad is under the CAR control as L1 reset default. Software programs the PMC override register (PMC_IMPL_OSC_EDPD_OVER_0_OSC_CTRL_SELECT->1) to transfer control to the PMC. Once the control is transferred to the PMC, it continues to be under PMC control until the next L0/ L1 reset. The CLK_OK pin masks the mode detection mechanism in the pad after power-on-reset in order to mitigate risk when the AVDD rail of the pad is later cycled during an SC7 transition to save power. CLK_OK should not be changed from its default of 0 to avoid the pad mode from changing to bypass to crystal during a reset sequence. If the AVDD_OSC rail is not powered off and back on during a chip reset sequence, CLK_OK must be held at 0 for the bypass mode to work. Refer to the PMC_IMPL_OSC_EDPD_OVER register.
##### 4.2.3.1.2 Powering Down the OSC
The SC7 hardware sequencer proceeds to OSC_OFF state only if it is right to turn off OSC in SC7. The decision to turn off OSC is dependent on the following factors. No software overrides bits that disables OSC power down in SC7 are set. (PMC_IMPL_OSC_EDPD_OVER.XO_LP0_MODE). The AOPM signals to the PMC that OSC can be shut off. The high-level state of OSC_OFF consists of the following hardware sequence on powering down the OSC: 1.
- Hand shake with the TSC to ensure that the switch over to the 32 kHz clock is complete
within the TSC. The PMC sends a clock switch request to MTSC, which is acknowledged by
- TSC by asserting an ack to PMC. Note: The TSC is required to acknowledge the switch
request irrespective of the TSC configuration settings. Assert an OSC stable indication to cleanly gate off the undivided OSC clock within AO CAR. This step is required to ensure that there are no clock glitches propagated to active logic when the OSC pad is disabled. The CAR clock gating logic uses this OSC stable indication for clock gating. De-assert EN_XO to OSC pad after at least one 32 kHz clock cycle. 2. 3. When the SC7 state is exited, following sequence is required to be done in OSC_ON state. 1. Assert EN_XO to reenable the OSC pad.

- PMC Programming Guidelines
2.
- Wait for OSC_PREPWR delay expiry in the PMC_IMPL_PWRGOOD_TIMER_0 register. If there
is a valid wake-requiring VDD_CORE to be powered up, SOC_PWR_REQ is asserted and the PWRGOOD timer starts.
- OSC_POSTPWR delay and assert the OSC stable indication. CAR logic uses this signal to
ungate the OSC clock path. Perform handshake with TSC to switch the MTSC clock back to the OSC clock. 3. 4. When the SoC is in SC7, the AOPM module can request the OSC power-up when wake events (such as Tier 0, RTC alarm timeout, or other indications like nWFE, nWFI, nCLKSTOPPED) are received by the AOPM. When this occurs, SC7 sequencer completes the OSC startup steps specified preceding and waits for either: 1.
- An OSC power down request from the AOPM. For example, the PD bit of the oscillator, but
not the rail. Completion of the SC7 exit when a valid wake event is seen. 2.
- The timing diagram below shows the key actions involved in enabling the OSC module when a
wake-up condition is detected. OSC_PREPWR and POSTPWR timers take effect only when SC7 reaches OSC_OFF state.
**Figure 4.32 SC7 Sequencer Timing Diagram**

- PMC Programming Guidelines
#### 4.2.3.2 Wake Engine Programming
##### 4.2.3.2.1 Wake Configuration
The wake engine supports the following wake-specific configuration: 1.
- Wake-signaling parameters: These include the wake polarity, filter/de-bounce settings as
applicable. These signaling parameters could be platform-dependent and need to comprehend specific wake signal properties (for example, CAN wakes)
- Wake coalescing configuration (coalescing enable, coalescing group selection)
- Wake masks and wake status indication
- Wake routing configuration
2. 3. 4. The wake-specific configuration handled in software, for the wake engine to detect wakeup events and trigger SC7 exit is as follows: 1. 2. 3. 4. 5. 6. Enable signaling parameters for all wakes. Enable coalescing on all Tier1 and Tier2 wakes. Program group 0 timer with a value that meets PMIC sequencing requirements. Map all Tier1 and Tier2 wakes to group 0 window. Route wake events to any of three tiers. Unmask wake events.
##### 4.2.3.2.2 Delay Buffer Selection
A programmable number of delay chains were used to implement the delay filter logic. In the worst case, the requirement must reach at least ~2 ns delay to support glitch filtering. Before wake is enabled, the WAKE_AOWAKE_DELAY_CELL_CTRL_0_SIG_DELAY_BUF_SEL register must be configured with a tap select value based on per tap delays. This register must be programmed to 14 (hex value: E) to meet 2 ns delay.
##### 4.2.3.2.3 Wake Coalescing
The wake coalescing logic has hooks for software to enable/disable coalescing, to map wakes to different groups, and to program group timers to hold wakes based on wake latency tolerance.
- Enabling coalescing and group selection is handled through WAKE_AOWAKE_CTRL_x, which is
assigned per wake event. There are global timers for each group window. These timers can be programmed through WAKE_AOWAKE_COAL_GRP0/1_0.
- WAKE DELAY Implementation
SOC_PWR_REQ is a side band signal of the SoC that goes to the PMIC to control the SoC rail. When this sideband is de-asserted in SC7, there are specific platform considerations, which prevent the

- PMC Programming Guidelines
rail turn ON, before a certain delay has elapsed. Hence, any Tier1 or Tier2 wake event that leads to the SC7 exit is not exposed to the SC7 exit sequencer during this window. On earlier chips, this functionality is achieved using the WAKE_DELAY timer. The following programming is required in the SoC: 1. 2. Enable coalescing on all Tier1 and Tier2 wakes.
- Group 0 timer (smaller window) needs to be programmed with a minimum value of SoC turn
off delay mentioned preceding. All the Tier1 and Tier2 wakes needs to be mapped to this smaller window by default. 3. This ensures that all Tier1 and Tier2 wakes are held and not seen on the interrupt lines before this minimum SoC turn off delay. Based on wake latency tolerances, wakes can be mapped to the larger window (group 1) to increase the residency in SC7 state. Since the group 0 timer is used as a workaround for wake delay feature, this timer is not available for generic coalescing feature described in the Wake Coalescing section.
##### 4.2.3.2.4 Global Disable Control for Wake Coalescing
The coalescing output on each wake line is triggered when the corresponding coalescing window expires and wake status bit is set. Coalescing timers are implemented so that they are free running only in SC7 i.e., across PWR_OFF and PWR_ON state of the SC7 sequencer. Any wake that is triggered after PWR_ON state or in SC0 is not seen on the interrupt lines until coalescing is disabled. The WAKE_AOWAKE_CNTRL_0_GLOBAL_COAL_EN bit can be used to disable coalescing on all wakes on SC7 exit. This bit should be LOW in order to do this. Individual COAL_EN takes effect when set to 1. However, wake status registers indicate the right wake-up status of all wake events occurred until then. In SC0, i.e., while the system is in active state, if a wake interrupt needs to be detected: WAKE_DET_EN should be enabled. Coalescing must be disabled on all wakes.
##### 4.2.3.2.5 Wake Register Isolation
Each wake event can be assigned to a specific owner group through its corresponding SCR setting.
- All SCRs are set up during BL-MB1 for NV-owned wake-up sources and at BL-MB2 for OEM owned
wake-up sources. The SCR organization for wake-specific registers is shown in the figure below.

- PMC Programming Guidelines
**Figure 4.33 SCR Organization for Wake Specific Registers**
The MASK/STATUS/CNTRL registers corresponding to the wake event can be assigned to their own groups matching the wake event ownership. The SCR organization for wake routing registers is shown in the figure below.

- PMC Programming Guidelines
**Figure 4.34 SCR Organization for Wake Routing Registers**
Tier0/1/2 specific routing registers are owned by SPE/BPMP/CPU respectively. Additionally, Tier 2 routing registers should have read privileges set for BPMP through SCRs as BPMP needs to check the wake status and tier routing configuration on SC7 exit. This is to know if the wake event is a Tier1/2 wake in order to conclude on whether to reenter SC7 or exit SC7-CC7 to SC0-CC0 or SC0- CC7.

- PMC Programming Guidelines
**Figure 4.35 SCR Organization for RO Status and Mask Registers**
##### 4.2.3.2.6 Wake Routing
Wake engine has software hooks to route a wake to any of the wake-handling processors in the system. For example: SPE, BPMP, and CPU. These tier-specific wake routing registers must be set up to direct a specific wake to a tier master.
- WAKE_AOWAKE_TIER0_ROUTING_31_0_0
- WAKE_AOWAKE_TIER0_ROUTING_63_32_0
- WAKE_AOWAKE_TIER0_ROUTING_95_64_0
- WAKE_AOWAKE_TIER1_ROUTING_31_0_0
- WAKE_AOWAKE_TIER1_ROUTING_63_32_0
- WAKE_AOWAKE_TIER1_ROUTING_95_64_0
- WAKE_AOWAKE_TIER2_ROUTING_31_0_0
- WAKE_AOWAKE_TIER2_ROUTING_63_32_0
- WAKE_AOWAKE_TIER2_ROUTING_95_64_0
0: Do not route the corresponding wake event to Tier_x wake 1: Route the corresponding wake event to Tier_x wake
##### 4.2.3.2.7 Tier1/2 Wakes as SPE interrupts
- Interrupt (pmc2vic_intr) can be raised to SPE on a valid wake by setting
- WAKE_AOWAKE_TIER1/2_CTRL_0_INT_EN. This notifies the SPE that a Tier1 or 2 wake occurred
leading to SC7 exit.
##### 4.2.3.2.8 Wake Promotion
The wake engine supports the ability to promote a wake to a different tier dynamically. For example, to promote a specific wake in Tier0 category to Tier1/2, the SPE can update respective fields in the WAKE_AOWAKE_TIER1/2_ROUTING registers. Once this register is updated, the wake status propagates as the wake event to the desired master. On a high level, the sequence of actions in this scenario would be:
- SPE receives Tier0 Wake interrupt

- PMC Programming Guidelines
- SPE does not clear the status bit
- SPE updates Tier1/2 wake routing registers
The wake event is now enabled as a Tier1/2 wake interrupt, which will wake up the BPMP/CCPLEX. In this case, the SCRs for the Tier1/2 wake routing registers must be set up so that the SPE can access those registers. Also, the BPMP/CCPLEX must have access to the wake registers specific to this Tier0 wake (i.e., CNTRL, MASK, and STATUS), if BPMP/CCPLEX must clear the status bit. During wake initialization, wake events can statically be routed to multiple tiers as well. In this case, wake-specific configuration can be handled by either of the masters. SCRs should be set up accordingly.
##### 4.2.3.2.9 Wake Masking and Status
- The WAKE_AOWAKE_MASK_W_x register can be used to unmask/mask the desired wake lines. This
register is assigned per wake event. By default, all the wake events are masked. The wake status post masking is captured in the WAKE_AOWAKE_STATUS_R_x registers. The wake status can be cleared by writing to the WAKE_AOWAKE_STATUS_W_x_CLEAR registers. This register is assigned per wake event. These wake status registers are also cleared by the PMC hardware during the SC7 entry provided that WAKE_DET_EN is not set. If WAKE_DET_EN is set, software can clear these registers. If software does not enable wake detection, the wake event gets reflected in the wake status register only on the SC7 exit (WAIT_FOR_DPD_DIS) state.
- The wake engine also has a second set of status registers under software control. The
- WAKE_AOWAKE_SW_STATUS_R_x registers are used to latch the wake status without mask
control. These registers reflect true wake-up status even outside of the SC7 provided that DET_EN is set. Software can clear the status of all wakes by writing to the
- WAKE_AOWAKE_SW_STATUS_W_0_CLEAR register. The SC7 sequencer cannot clear these
registers. WAKE_AOWAKE_LATCH_SW_0_LATCH_SWEN needs to be enabled to latch wakeup events into these registers.
##### 4.2.3.2.10 WAKE_DET_EN
By default, wake detection is not enabled and so, none of the wakes get detected after boot. While entering SC7, wake detection is enabled in hardware on entering the ASSERT_CLAMP state of the SC7 sequencer. In order to capture the events that occur outside of SC7, software needs to enable wake detection by setting the WAKE_AOWAKE_DET_EN register. Along with the wake events in SC7, setting this bit ensures that the following are captured:
- The events that could occur before the hardware enters SC7 state, but after software has
instructed hardware to enter the state
- Events occur after hardware wake-up, but before software has enabled the peripherals that
process the wake-up events

- PMC Programming Guidelines
While setting or changing the wake configuration, wake detection needs to be disabled first. Configure all wake settings and then enable detection.
##### 4.2.3.2.11 Timestamping of Wake Events
- Software can program WAKE_AOWAKE_TSC_CTRL_0_WAKE_INDEX to indicate which event to
select for TSC snap. This resets the TSC snap value to 0.The snap value gets incremented once that specific wake status gets updated. The snap value is latched in WAKE_AOWAKE_TSC_SNAP_VALUE_0.
#### 4.2.3.3 Thermtrip Programming Guidelines
##### 4.2.3.3.1 Direct Shutdown on Thermtrip
The PMC optionally asserts the shutdown pin to the off-chip PMIC when a thermtrip alert triggers.
- This thermtrip alert can come either from SoC THERM or FSI THERM. The PMIC treats the
- SHUTDOWN_N sideband as a failsafe trigger for shutting the system down. Then, the user
manually turns the system on by pressing the power button or equivalent inputs. The PMC provides a configuration bit PMC_IMPL_DIRECT_THERMTRIP_CONFIG_THERMTRIP_EN to enable the failsafe shutdown option. When the THERMTRIP_EN bit is set, the PMC asserts the internal reset when it asserts SHUTDOWN_N but does not de-assert the internal reset when the source of thermtrip is cleared in hardware. The system software can choose to enable a failsafe shutdown or continue with the Boot ROM-based legacy shutdown solution.
- The PMC does not power gate the CPU partitions on a thermtrip alert. CPU_PWR_REQ is de-
asserted because of L1 reset, so CCPLEX is rail-gated. SHUTDOWN_N is always an active low signal from the SoC perspective. This pin is driven LOW only when the SoC wants to shut down the system. At all other times, this output is tri-stated. This flexibility allows other external platform components to assert the shutdown pin to the PMIC.
- The internal system reset events do not affect the SHUTDOWN_N pin state. The pin, when
asserted, reverts to its default when external chip reset (SYS_RESET_N) is asserted or on the expiry of SHDN_ASSERT_PULSE_WIDTH counter, whichever is earlier. The DPD controls for this pad are tied OFF to never enter DPD mode.
- Note: The SHUTDOWN_N output is always treated as an active LOW signal, and the platform
enables the appropriate external pull ups on these signals. If the PMIC supports an OTP option to choose the polarity of the shutdown input, it is critical that this setting is configured to enable ACTIVE LOW operation.

- PMC Programming Guidelines
**Figure 4.36 THERMTRIP Sequence**
#### 4.2.3.4 Power Gating Controller
Power-gating logic in PMC handles the following cases from the SRAM and logic power control point of view.
##### 4.2.3.4.1 Boot/Reset Requirements
Boot/Reset requirements on PMC PG HW:
- PMC ensures that all Power-gate-able Power domains on SoC, CV rails except the XUSB
domain on SoC rail are in power-gated state on all cold and warm resets.
- XUSB power domain alone needs to be brought up in functional state on all cold and warm
boot cycles. All AON RAMs need to be brought to functional mode on all flavors of cold boot cycles. This is ensured by asynchronously asserting the following controls on any reset deassertion in the following order:
- Assert the power down request
- Assert the power gating clamp
- Assert power gating controls (except XUSB) controls such that both logic and RAMs are in
- SLEEP mode
Power-gating status registers are also updated accordingly. It is Boot software or runtime FW responsibility to power ungate relevant Power domains as per the use case.

- PMC Programming Guidelines
During SC7 entry, as per the definition of AON power states, these RAMs are expected to be put in SLEEP/RET mode. During exit, it is SC7 exit FW responsibility to ensure the RAMs are in functional mode before they are accessed. Irrespective of the hardware actions to bring RAMs out of functional mode on reset deassertion, current scheme recommended to Boot ROM is to write POWER GATING REGISTERS corresponding to the RAMs required for booting. If the RAMs happen to be in functional mode already, it should just be a NOP. The Boot ROM has unconditionally written to the register to bring RAMs to active state in each boot path, regardless anyway, including when it is not needed like L0 reset.
##### 4.2.3.4.2 Power Gating Scenarios
If logic in a partition is required to be powered off, software should request for both LOGIC_SLEEP as well as SRAM_SLEEP or SRAM_RET. When a partition is requested to be power gated off completely using the preceding controls, the PMC logic makes sure that the logic sleep and SRAM SLEEP controls are sequenced in the correct way. The SRAM SLEEP controls are asserted first, before asserting the logic sleep controls while power gating. Similarly, when the partition is power ungated, the logic sleep controls are de-asserted before bringing SRAMs out of SLEEP mode. If the software programs use only the LOGIC_SLEEP bit to power off a partition, then the PMC hardware asserts the SRAM SLEEP controls and only then asserts LOGIC_SLEEP controls. During such an illegal request from software, the PMC can raise an interrupt to LIC, if enabled using the PMC_IMPL_PMC2LIC_INTR_ENABLE_0_ILLEGAL_SRAM_LOGIC_POWER_STATE bit.
- The following table summarizes the types of power gating actions supported and the PMC
involvement in these actions.
- Table 4.22 Power Gating Actions
- Power Gating Type
- Definition
- SoC NPG
Logic Not Power Gated; no power gating controls from PMC.
- SoC PG
- Logic Can be Power Gated; SRAMs can be put in SLEEP mode by the
software through PMC.
- AO-PG
- Logic in AO domain power gated by the PMC upon receiving request from
the local hardware. The PMC provides software-controlled RAM SLEEP/RET controls. The local hardware requests the PMC to put TCMs/Caches in RET mode.
- AO-NPG
Logic in AO not power gated. The PMC provides RAM SLEEP/RET controls.
- CV-PG
- Logic in the CV can be power gated. PMC provides RAM SLEEP and LOGIC
SLEEP controls. PMC does not drive any controls to CV-SRAM(FCM-based). The PG controller follows a priority order to avoid race conditions from requests coming from the software. The SC7 hardware sequencer and the AOPM hardware sequencer undo SLEEP/RET commands on reset deassertion.

- PMC Programming Guidelines
##### 4.2.3.4.3 Software Interface for Power Gating
The PMC supports one register per power domain for power gating support. Software can specify the target power state for logic and the SRAMs in each partition through the
- PMC_IMPL_<PART>_POWER_GATE_CONTROL register. Clamp control registers are supported
separately. Power gating software asserts the clamp controls and reset/clock gating controls (located in CAR) as required to accomplish entry into and out of power-gated states. None of the timer/configuration settings should be changed when power gating hardware is active (i.e., one or more PMC_IMPL_<PART>_POWER_GATE_CONTROL.START bits are set). Software requests for a SRAM/Logic-low power mode by setting the START bit. The START bit should always be set after configuring the target power state.
- The power-gating control logic samples the requested power state information in the
- PMC_IMPL_<PART>POWER_GATE_CONTROL register. Setting the START bit validates the request
for power control management. Though software can set up multiple partitions for power gating, the power gating sequencer handles only one request from the software at one time. Similarly, the PMC_POWER_GATE_STATUS register reflects the status of the supported power controls. All the fields marked here are not applicable to all the power gating partitions. For SoC, CV, PG partitions, SRAM_RET_EN, and the corresponding status register is reserved. For AON RAMs,
- LOGIC_SLEEP_EN, and CLAMP controls and the status bits are reserved. There is no software
control for power gating the AOPG partition. The AOPM can request the PMC to power gate it during the AON deep dormant state. When software requests a power mode entry, which is identical to the present power mode, the sequencer ignores the request. For example, the hardware sequencer does not re-sequence the controls to enter the mode. However, if the respective status bit is cleared in the
- PMC_IMPL_POWER_GATE_STATUS register, hardware sets this bit again in response to the new
request. To simplify the hardware design of the controller, it is required that software always requests power mode transitions, in a consistent manner as far as all the partition power controls are concerned. For example, it is illegal to request a state transition in a single request, which takes the SRAMs out of SLEEP and also asserts SRAM_RET and LOGIC_SLEEP. In other words, requests that flip the PMC_IMPL_POWER_GATE_CONTROL [3:0] bits in the opposite direction (0 ->1 and 1 ->0) in a single request are not supported. When software requests for multiple power gating actions, there is no specific arbitration scheme implemented in the hardware; it depends on the micro-architectural implementation.
##### 4.2.3.4.4 AON RAM PG/UPG Sequence
The following is the sequence for bringing RAMs out of low-power states. 1. Set the power state for the <AORAM> to OFF state.

- PMC Programming Guidelines
a.
- Kick off the PG state machine in PMC by writing
- PMC_IMPL_PART_<AORAM>_POWER_GATE_CONTROL register for that power domain
with: i.
- SRAM_SLEEP = OFF
- SRAM_RET = OFF
- INTER_PART_DELAY_EN = ENABLE
- START = 1
ii. iii. iv. 2.
- Poll PMC_IMPL_PART_<AORAM> _POWER_GATE_CONTROL register until START==0. If the
- START!=0 even after 200us, then flag ERROR
- Read PMC_IMPL_PART_<AORAM>_POWER_GATE_STATUS register to ensure that desired
state is reached without any error flags. Verify that the status fields read as follows. 3. a. b.
- SRAM_SLEEP_STS == OFF
- SRAM_RET_STS == OFF
If there is a mismatch, flag ERROR. <AORAM> in the preceding sequence maps to: 1. 2. 3. 4. 5. “SCRATCH” for PMC scratch RAM “MSS” for MSS_AON Scratch RAM “AONPG” for MSS Encryption RAM “TZRAM” for AON TZRAM RAMs. “DBBRAM” for AON DBB RAMs Note that the LOGIC_SLEEP and CLAMP Controls are defunct for AON RAMs.
##### 4.2.3.4.5 Power Control Sequencing
Below is the sequence to signal a specific partition control (xyz) over the muxed zone bus. This low- level sequencer is triggered for staggering RAM and LOGIC SLEEP_EN bus in a staggered manner.
- This sequence manipulates one control (F_LOGIC_SLEEP or F_SRAM_SLEEP) at one time, for the
partition being managed. The other controls (F_* signals) specific to this partition stays at the default value (of 01) or the last-sequenced value. 1. Set the zone bus to the appropriate initial value (00 when asserting a control, FF when de- asserting the control). Wait for Tzone2force delay. F_xyz [1:0] -> 00. This enables the sampling of the zone bus at the destination. Wait for Tforce2zone delay.
- If zoning is enabled for this control (as defined in PMC_ZONE_CONFIG register), start the
zone signaling and stop at the last zone value (FF or 00 as applicable). Zone timers define the time window between state changes. 2. 3. 4. 5.

- PMC Programming Guidelines
6. If zoning is not enabled for this control, the zone bus moves directly from 0x00 to 0xFF (or vice versa). Wait for Tzone2force delay. F_xyz [1:0] -> 01 (to force signal xyz LOW) or 10 (to force signal xyz high). Wait for Tforce2zone delay. 7. 8. 9.
- Certain power domains can contain multiple partitions. When no interpartition delay is
enabled for such power domains (i.e., PMC_IMPL_ <PART>_POWER_GATE_ CONTROL.
- INTER_PART_DELAY_EN = 0), the PG sequencer treats the entire power domain as a single
partition and goes through the individual control handling in parallel. When interpartition delay is enabled for such power domains, the power control of each of the partitions are sequentially handled (steps 1 through 8 preceding), with a delay (defined by
- INTER_PART_DELAY) inserted between each individual sequence. The clamp signal (driven
out of PMC_IMPL_<PART>_CLAMP_CONTROL register) is power domain specific.
#### 4.2.3.5 Pad Control Programming
##### 4.2.3.5.1 DPD Request
The PMC_IMPL_IO_DPD_REQ_0 register is a DPD request register that puts I/O rails in DPD mode or out of DPD mode, even if the chip in not in SC7. Multiple bits are allowed to be set at the same time and no new operation is triggered until the previous one is completed. Consecutive operations, issued by the completion time of the first one, are dropped but the register is still updated. After writing to the IO_DPD_REQ register, software should wait before writing to the same register again (after reading the status). There is no wait required to write between one IO_DPD_REQ register and the others. This is because there is a separate sequencer for every such register. There is a timing relationship between sel_dpd assertion to e_dpd assertion (similarly sel_dpd deassertion to e_dpd deassertion). This is controlled by a programmable timer (PMC_IMPL_SEL_DPD_TIM_0) in the PMC. When the IO_DPD_REQ register is written, sel_dpd of the corresponding pads get asserted and after the SEL_DPD_TIM delay expiry, e_dpd gets asserted. The state machine goes to idle only after this. So, the time between consecutive writes to IO_DPD_REQ is:
- APB clock frequency *(SEL_DPD_TIM + 5)
- The same delay is applicable before software reads the IO_DPD*_STATUS register after the
corresponding IO_DPD*_REQ register is written.

- PMC Programming Guidelines
SEL_DPD_TIM should be set to a safe value as there is a single timer for all pad groups. It can also be lowered, if the APB clock is slower (a minimum 200 ns is required).
##### 4.2.3.5.2 Pad DPD Sequence
Ensure that the PMC_IMPL_SEL_DPD_TIM_0 register is set to recommended value.
- Software can set multiple IO_DPD_REQ registers bits at the same time, indicating a request
to put multiple I/Os into DPD.
- CODE field of IO_DPD_REQ register indicates whether the transition is into or out of DPD
modes. PMC supports separate DPD sequencing logic for each IO_DPD_REQ register.
- PMC DPD sequencing logic will service each set of controls concurrently, until all pending
requests are complete. When a set of DPD sequencing is complete the respective bit will be updated in the IO_DPD_STATUS register.
#### 4.2.3.6 Voltage Monitor Reset and Interrupt Enabling Guidelines
- PMC_IMPL_VFMON_ACTION_0_VMON_EN should always be set to 1 (by reset default
VMON_EN is set to 1, already), for the logic in the PMC to capture masking or to enable reset/ interrupt actions. Irrespective of the action selection, PMC_IMPL_VFMON_STATUS_0 captures the fault status. Writing 1 to this register clears it. Reset enable: To enable VMON faults for generating legacy and/or async resets:
- Each of the minimum and maximum violation has a corresponding bit in
PMC_IMPL_VFMON_ACTION_0 register that needs to be set to RST. In addition, there is a global bit per each rail that is monitored, i.e., one bit for VDD_CORE,
- VDD_CPU0 and VDD_CPU1 rails in PMC_IMPL_L0L1A_RST_SOURCE_EN_0 which needs to
be enabled.
- Interrupt enable: To enable vfmon_intr on any of voltage faults, the corresponding bit in
PMC_IMPL_VFMON_ACTION_0 needs to be set to INTR.
- Interrupt mask: In addition, there are PMC_IMPL_VFMON_INT_MASK_0 register bits that can
be used to mask a fault that can assert this interrupt.

- PMC Programming Guidelines
#### 4.2.3.7 Frequency Monitor Programming Guidelines
**Figure 4.37 FMON Reset/Interrupt/Fault Connectivity**
- Reset_Action/HSM_Action are from FMON_FAULT_ACTION register
- Interrupt_Action is from VFMON_ACTION register
- Report[3:0] are from FMON_CONFIG register
Direct DC reset request connections are not shown. Refer to the Clock and Reset chapter for clock monitoring details.
##### 4.2.3.7.1 FMON Error Reporting
- The following sequence is written for OSC FMON. The same sequence applies to 32 kHz FMON
(replace OSCnFUSE_CK with PMC_CK in the register/field names). FMON can monitor low threshold violations, high threshold violations, overflow errors, and DC clock stoppage faults. The following register fields must be enabled for reporting the preceding faults. These bits for OSC and 32 kHz are enabled by default and are always kept enabled.
- PMC_IMPL_FMON_CONFIG_OSCnFUSE_CK_0
- FMON_REPORT_DC_FAULT_VIOL_OSCnFUSE_CK_0 for reporting clock stoppage fault
- FMON_REPORT_HIGH_THRESH_VIOL_OSCnFUSE_CK_0 for reporting fault if there is high
threshold violation
- FMON_REPORT_LOW_THRESH_VIOL_OSCnFUSE_CK_0 for reporting fault if there is a low
threshold violation FMON_REPORT_OVERFLOW_ERROR_OSCnFUSE_CK_0 for overflow errors.

- PMC Programming Guidelines
##### 4.2.3.7.2 Enable Reset Request Path from FMONs
- The following sequence is written for OSC FMON. The same sequence applies to 32 kHz FMON
(replace OSCnFUSE_CK with PMC_CK in the register/field names).
- PMC_IMPL_FMON_FAULT_ACTION_OSCnFUSE_CK [0] = 1
This alone enables a reset request path due to all four faults (including clock stop fault) from the OSC FMON. A similar bit exists for 32 kHz FMON- PMC_IMPL_FMON_FAULT_ACTION_PMC_CK [0]. If there is a case where the reset request must be enabled due to clock stoppage alone, but not the other faults like low/high threshold violations, then
- PMC_IMPL_FMON_FAULT_ACTION_OSCnFUSE_CLK[2] = 1
- PMC_IMPL_FMON_FAULT_ACTION_OSCnFUSE_CLK[0] = 0
- In addition, there is PMC_IMPL_L0L1A_RST_SOURCE_EN[SW_OSCRSTREQ], which the
software uses to generate a reset request. For regular sequence of enabling reset request path from FMONs, this register control need not be programmed.
##### 4.2.3.7.3 Enable FAULT and INTERRUPT Path from FMON
- The following sequence is written for OSC FMON. The same sequence applies to 32 kHz FMON
(replace OSCnFUSE_CK with PMC_CK in the register/field names).
- Enable Interrupts and Faults
1.
- Set
- PMC_IMPL_FMON_FAULT_ACTION_OSCnFUSE_CK_0[FMON_ACTION_FAULT_REPORT_OSCnF
USE_CK_0] to ENABLE. This enables the fault_out_pulse from FMON.
- Set PMC_IMPL_VFMON_ACTION_0[FOSC_FAULT_ACTION] to INTR. This enables both
interrupt and fault to HSM.
- To explicitly mask the interrupt and enable only fault to HSM, set
- PMC_IMPL_VFMON_INT_MASK_0[FOSC_FAULT] to MASK. This masks the interrupt line,
keeping the fault line enabled. 2. 3.
- FMON Threshold Settings
- The following sequence is written for OSC FMON The same sequence applies to 32 kHz FMON
(replace OSCnFUSE_CK with PMC_CK in the register/field names). By default, for OSC and 32 kHz FMONs, threshold settings are set assuming +/- 50% inaccuracy in VREFRO clock. These registers use L1A cold reset. Therefore, during L0 and L1A boot, these registers are reset to default values. During boot, once VREFRO calibration is complete, the threshold values must be programmed such that the clocks can be monitored with a much higher accuracy. VREFRO accuracy after calibration is at 5%. Overall, the clock monitoring accuracy requirement is 10%. During the L1B, L1C, and L2 boot paths, both the calibration settings for VREFRO in the CAR page, as well as FMON threshold settings in the PMC, are not reset. There are maintained at +/-10% margins.

- PMC Registers
For details, refer to the Clock Controller chapter.
### 4.2.4 PMC Registers
Refer to "Reading Register Tables" in the Introduction chapter for the register table protocol as well as recommendations for accessing registers. All PMC configuration registers are implemented in the APB clock domain. Read/write access to these registers does not result in any wait state generation on the APB bus.

- Reset
- Description
31:0 0x0
- RESERVED
- PMC_IMPL_DPD_ENABLE_0
Deep Power Down Enable Setting this register will trigger SC7 HW Sequencer.
- SC7 HW Sequencer turns off VDD_SOC rail, clamps interfaces to AON domain. Power gate AOPG
domain and can turn off OSC. Wake events and SC7 FSM Related registers are expected to be set up before writing to this bit. After serving wakeup event, the register should be set back to 0 to complete SC7 cycle.

- PMC IMPL Registers
- PMC_IMPL_SC7_STATUS_0
- If SW wants to check for SC7 residency, it should check for SC_STATE (this corresponds to
soc_wake_req). If SW wants to check for sc7 FSM idle-ness , it should check for SC7_FSM_BUSY SC7 FSM may be non-idle, but system may still not be in SC7, since true SC7 happens when all steps - assert SRAM_SLEEP, assert clamp, PWROFF happen. In those states FSM will be non-idle, but SC_STATE may still be NONE.

0 = FALSE 1 = TRUE
- FALSE

for DPD_EN to be deasserted by SW 0 = FALSE 1 = TRUE
- FALSE
SC7_FSM_BUSY:
- Indicates whether SC7 FSM is in idle or not (idle == Not Busy, else Busy)
0 = FALSE 1 = TRUE 1:0

- PMC_IMPL_PWRGOOD_TIMER_0
Power Good Timer Programs length of wakeup reset, asserted after wakeup from lp0. The register should be set before entering lp0 mode. Programmed values depends on properties of power management unit. Timer value x 30.51 us = reset pulse length Increased the width of PWRGOOD timer to 16 bits.

- Parity Protection: Y
- Shadow: N

- Bit
- Reset
- Description
31:24 0x3f OSC_PREPWR: OSC clock stabilization timer prior to SoC rail pwr-req assertion.
- Timer value is 4*OSC_PREPWR+1 number of 32.768kHz clock cycles
i.e. timer value is (OSC_PREPWR*122.07)+30.518 usec. 23:16 0x0 OSC_POSTPWR: OSC clock stabilization timer after SoC rail power is stabilized.
- Timer value is 4*OSC_POSTPWR+1 number of 32.768kHz clock cycles
i.e. timer value is (OSC_POSTPWR*122.07)+30.518 usec.

- FUSE_CONTROL
- Offset: 0x104

- Shadow: N

- Bit
- Reset
- Description
0x0 THERMTRIP_LOCK: When set to 1, locks THERMTRIP_EN and AOTAG THERMTRIP threshold.
- This lock bit is expected to write-lock all register bits that can disable or
sabotage direct shutdown.
- Write-once Updated by secure SW after setting all direct shutdown
thermtrip related registers. 0 = DISABLE 1 = ENABLE 0x1 THERMTRIP_EN:
- When this bit is set, then PMC will assert SHUTDOWN sideband to PMIC
on a thermal sensor reset event.
- The system will then be shutdown directly by PMIC instead of causing a
shutdown through BootROM. This configuration bit will be cleared only by an external reset.
- The thermal sensor reset request can come from SOC_therm or from the
internal AOTAG in PMC. SOC_therm will not be able to send a reset request while in LP0 or LP0BB.
- The internal AOTAG will be capable of sending a thermtrip alert in LP0 or
LP0BB. This field overrides PMC_SENSOR_CTRL_ENABLE_RST. 0 = DISABLE 1 = ENABLE 3:0 0x0 SHDN_ASSERT_PULSE_WIDTH:
- SHUTDOWN pin, once asserted by PMC, remains asserted for
theprogrammed number of 32K clock cycles.
- This field is cleared by external reset only

- PMC_IMPL_RST_REQ_CONFIG_0
- For the RST_REQ_CONFIG and RST_REQ_CNTVAL registers - the configuration variables for each
reset level are reset using a reset one level lower. Example:
- L1a configurations knobs are reset using L0 cold register
- L1b configurations knobs are reset using L1a cold register
- L1c configurations knobs are reset using L1b cold register
- L2 configurations knobs are reset using L1c cold register
- WDT_OUT_RST_EN fields that enable WDT_RESET_OUT - should NOT be written by SW. It is
supposed to be set only in bootcode.
- Offset: 0x114
- Read/Write: R/W
- Parity Protection: Y
- Shadow: N
- SCR Protection: PMC_IMPL_SCR_CNTRL_SCR_0
- Reset: 0x00000000 (0bxxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,0x00)
- Bit
- Reset
- Description
- DISABLE
L1CRST_WDT_OUT_RST_EN: Enables Sideband WDT_RESET_OUT for SW resetcases.
- Should only be used with PMIC that support RESET_IN
0 = DISABLE 1 = ENABLE
- DISABLE
L1BAOWDTRST_WDT_OUT_RST_EN: Enables Sideband WDT_RESET_OUT for AOWDT usecases.
- Should only be used with PMIC that support RESET_IN
0 = DISABLE 1 = ENABLE

- PMC_IMPL_RST_REQ_CNTVAL_0
- Reset level: one reset level lower than the reset it generates
- Offset: 0x118
- Read/Write: R/W
- Parity Protection: Y
- Shadow: N
- SCR Protection: PMC_IMPL_SCR_CNTRL_SCR_0
- Reset: 0x04000000 (0b0000,0100,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000)
- PROD: 0x04040404 (0b0000,0100,0000,0100,0000,0100,0000,0100)
- Bit
- Reset
- PROD
- Description
31:24 0x4 0x4 L2RST:
- IST/BOOT SW should make sure that the value is more than
4 before enterting into IST. Number of pmc_clk (32K) cycles before L2 reset deassertion 23:16 0x0 0x4 L1CRST:
- IST/BOOT SW should make sure that the value is more than
4 before enterting into IST. Number of pmc_clk (32K) cycles before L1c reset deassertion 15:8 0x0 0x4 L1BRST:
- IST/BOOT SW should make sure that the value is more than
4 before enterting into IST. Number of pmc_clk (32K) cycles before L1b reset deassertion 7:0 0x0 0x4 L1ARST:
- Number of pmc_clk (32K) cycles before L1a reset
deassertion
- PMC_IMPL_VFMON_ACTION_0
- VFMON Registers
These are all RWTO because they need to be reset on L0 cold reset since VFMON causes an L1a reset.

- PMC_IMPL_VFMON_INT_STATUS_0

- PMC_IMPL_VFMON_INT_MASK_0
- Note that in order to raise an interrupt to LIC, INTR should be the selected action in
PMC_IMPL_VFMON_ACTION register and UNMASK corresponding field in this register.
- In addition to interrupts, OSC and 32KHz FMON can raise a fault to HSM. Selecting
VFMON_ACTION as INTR raises a fault to HSM, irrespective of the MASK bit. In addition make sure
- FMON_ACTION_FAULT_REPORT_* bit of PMC_IMPL_FMON_ACTION_* register is also enabled to
raise an interrupt/fault from FMONs.
- Offset: 0x1dc
- Read/Write: R/W
- Parity Protection: Y
- Shadow: N
- SCR Protection: PMC_IMPL_SCR_VFMON_ST_SCR_0
- Reset: 0x000003ff (0bxxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xx11,1111,1111)

- PMC_IMPL_POWER_GATE_TIMERS_0
- _POWER_GATE_CONTROL
- LOGIC_SLEEP : when set along with START set, PG partition will be kept in Power gated mode

- PMC IMPL Registers
(power to the partition is gated) : When reset along with START set, PG partition will be removed from Power gated mode and kept in Functional mode (power to the partition is un-gated) : When LOGIC_SLEEP is set without SRAM_SLEEP_EN and SRAM_RET_EN, SRAMs are kept in
- SLEEP mode as a bonus and an illegal interrutp is generated out of PMC
- SRAM_RET_EN : when set along with START set, SRAMs in partition will be kept in RETENTION
mode : When reset along with START set, SRAMs in partition will be moved to Functional mode : SRAM_SLEEP_EN has higher priority than SRAM_RET_EN : When LOGIC_SLEEP is set without SRAM_SLEEP_EN and SRAM_RET_EN, SRAMs are kept in
- SLEEP mode as a bonus and an illegal interrutp is generated out of PMC
: This works as per-SRAM control for AO SRAM_SLEEP_EN : when set along with START set, SRAMs in partition will be kept in SLEEP mode : When reset along with START set, SRAMs in partition will be moved to Functional mode : SRAM_SLEEP_EN has higher priority than SRAM_RET_EN : When LOGIC_SLEEP is set without SRAM_SLEEP_EN and SRAM_RET_EN, SRAMs are kept in
- SLEEP mode as a bonus and an illegal interrutp is generated out of PMC
: This works as per-SRAM control for AO
- START : Self clear bit to trigger operations
- _POWER_GATE_STATUS
- LOGIC_SLEEP_STS : Reflectes the current status of the Partition
: When read 1, Partition is in Logic sleep : When read 0, Partition is not in Logic sleep
- SRAM_RET_STS : Reflectes the current status of the SRAMs in the Partition
: When read 1, SRAMs in Partition are in Retention mode : When read 0, SRAMs in Partition are not in Retention mode, check SRAM_SLEEP_STS : This works as per-SRAM status for AO : SW Overriden status is not reflected here
- SRAM_SLEEP_STS : Reflectes the current status of the SRAMs in the Partition
: When read 1, SRAMs in Partition are in SLEEP mode : When read 0, SRAMs in Partition are not in SLEEP mode, check SRAM_RET_STS : This works as per-SRAM status for AO : SW Overriden status is not reflected here

- Bit

- PWRDWN
H1X_ACK: 1 = PWRDWN 0 = PWRUP
- PWRDWN

- PMC_IMPL_PMC2LIC_INTR_STATUS_0
- PMC2LIC interrupt

- PMC IMPL Registers
- Offset: 0x800
- Read/Write: R/W
- Parity Protection: N
- Shadow: N
- SCR Protection: PMC_IMPL_SCR_CNTRL_SCR_0
- Reset: 0x00000000 (0bxxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xx00)
- Bit
- Reset
- Description
0x0 ILLEGAL_SRAM_LOGIC_POWER_STATE: Set when SW requests an illegal power control request to a partition. i.e. SRAM not in any power mode and logic sleep is requested. HW will handle this properly: automatically set SRAM into sleep mode.
- Writing "1" to this bit will cause the status cleared
0x0 UNSUPPORTED_PG_REQUEST:
- Set when SW requests a power gating scenario, which is not supported in
PG sequencer. i.e. Requested transition is to do some mixing transition of "do-ret/sleep/ lsleep" and "undo-ret/sleep/lsleep" HW will take the "do" PG as higher priority.
- Writing "1" to this bit will cause the status cleared
- PMC_IMPL_PMC2LIC_INTR_ENABLE_0

- Parity Protection: Y
- Shadow: N

- PMC_IMPL_RAMDUMP_CTL_STATUS2_0
- Offset: 0x8e8
- Read/Write: R/W
- Parity Protection: N
- Shadow: N
- SCR Protection: PMC_IMPL_SCR_RAMDUMP_COM2_SCR_0
- Reset: 0x00000000 (0bxxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxx0)
- Bit
- Reset
- Description
- DISABLE
RAMDUMP_EN:
- Ramdump enable. This bit is only writable when
SECURE_BOOT_MODE is 1. This bit enables/disables the RamDump state machine in PMC. 1 = ENABLE 0 = DISABLE
- PMC_IMPL_IO_SYS_DPD_REQ_0
Puts IO rails in dpd mode or out of dpd mode , even when chip is not in SC7 mode. Multiple bits are allowed to be set at the same time. There is one DPD Sequencer per IO_DPD_REQ register. All DPD requests keyyed in before setting CODE bit are sequenced at the same time. Note there is a single sample bit (CODE field) per IO_DPD_REQ register. No new operation wil be triggered until previous one completes. Consequtive operations issued before the completion time of first one, will be dropped, but register will be still updated. There is no wait required to write between DPD_REQ,
- DPD2_REQ, DPD7_REQ, DPD8_REQ as HW has been updated to execute the 4 instructions in
parallel through 4 different sequencers. After writing to IO_DPD_REQ register, S/W should wait for sometime before writing to the same register again (after reading the status) There is a timing relationship between sel_dpd assertion to e_dpd assertion (similarly sel_dpd deassertion to e_dpd deassertion). This is controlled by a programmable timer (SEL_DPD_TIM register in the same page). When IO_DPD_REQ register is written, sel_dpd of the corresponding pads get asserted and after the SEL_DPD_TIM delay expiry, e_dpd gets asserted. state machine goes to idle only after this. So, the time between consecutive writes to IO_DPD_REQ twice should be - apb clock frequency

- PMC IMPL Registers
multiplied by (SEL_DPD_TIM value plus few apb clocks). Say : apb clock frequency *(SEL_DPD_TIM + 5). Same delay is applicable before S/W reads IO_DPD*_STATUS register after the corresponding IO_DPD*_REQ is written SEL_DPD_TIM should be set to safe value, but it can be lowered if APB clock is slower. (minimum 200 ns required) Note that SEL_DPD_TIM has to be set first to the required value and only then key in DPD requests in IO_DPD_REQ registers. SEL_DPD_TIM is not expected to be changed while the sequencer is active.
- Offset: 0xe014
- Read/Write: R/W
- Parity Protection: Y
- Shadow: N
- SCR Protection: PMC_IMPL_SCR_IO_SYS_SCR_0

#### 4.2.4.2 PMC Wake Registers
- WAKE_AOWAKE_CNTRL_0
To optimize wake engine HW, all the signaling filters are not observed on all wake events in HW. Depending on the wake event behavior, relevant filters are implemented in HW. SW should enable these filters as per the above spec. This is an array of 96 identical register entries; the register fields below apply to each entry. Full register list is: WAKE_AOWAKE_CNTRL_<i>, among which <i> belongs to <0..95>.
- Offset: 0x0,..,0x17c
- Read/Write: R/W
- Parity Protection: N
- Shadow: N
- SCR Protection: WAKE_SCR_EVENT_CNTRL_SCR_0
- Reset: 0x00000108 (0bxxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,0000,0001,x00x,1000)
- Bit
- Reset
- Description
15:8 0x1 DEBOUNCE_VAL:
- This field is used to define the de-bounce value for the de-bounce
filter. This value is ignored if DEBOUNCE_EN is not set. This value translates to number of 1KHz or 32KHz cycles depending on the type of CLK_DEBOUCE INST.
- FALSE
COAL_EN:
- This field is used enable/disable coalescing feature for a given wake
event.
- SW is expected to always enable coalescing, once COAL_GRP_SEL and
COAL_GRP0, COAL_GRP1 are programmed. 0 = FALSE 1 = TRUE
- GROUP0
COAL_GRP_SEL: wake coalescing group selection. 0 = GROUP0 1 = GROUP1

- PMC Wake Registers
- Bit
- Reset
- Description
- HIGH
LEVEL: wake level. If input wake level matches with this register, input wake is forwarded to wake processing logic(signaling). First filter on the input wake in the wake signalling module 0 = LOW 1 = HIGH
- FALSE
DEBOUNCE_EN: debounce filter disable/enable. SW is expected to enable this only after programming DEBOUCE_VAL.Fourth filter on the input wake in the wake signaling module 0 = FALSE 1 = TRUE
- FALSE
SR_CAPTURE_EN: sr latch capture disable/enable. Third filter on the input wake in the wake signaling. 0 = FALSE 1 = TRUE
- FALSE
DELAY_FILTER_EN: delay filter disable/enable. Second filter on the input wake in the wake signalling module 0 = FALSE 1 = TRUE
- WAKE_AOWAKE_MASK_W_0
- One SCR per wake event
This is an array of 96 identical register entries; the register fields below apply to each entry. Full register list is: WAKE_AOWAKE_MASK_W_<i>, among which <i> belongs to <0..95>.
- Offset: 0x180,..,0x2fc
- Read/Write: WO
- Parity Protection: N
- Shadow: N
- SCR Protection: WAKE_SCR_EVENT_CNTRL_SCR_0
- Reset: 0x00000000 (0bxxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxx0)
- Bit
- Reset
- Description
- MASK
MASK: mask control for wake event. SW is expected to umask required wakes before SC7 entry. 0 = MASK 1 = UNMASK

- PMC Wake Registers

31:0 0x0 SEL: wake events(31-0) selection into tier0 wake routing. 0 means corresponding wake event not enabled for tier0 wake 1 means corresponding wake event is enabled for tier0 wake

- One SCR for the following register
- Offset: 0x4d8

- Parity Protection: N
- Shadow: N

- Reset: 0x00000000 (0bxxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxx0)
- Bit
- Reset
- Description
- FALSE
ENABLE: tier0 wake trigger by SW. SW can write this register with TRUE to trigger a wake event 0 = FALSE 1 = TRUE
- WAKE_AOWAKE_COAL_GRP0_0
- One SCR for the following two registers
- Offset: 0x4dc
- Read/Write: R/W
- Parity Protection: N
- Shadow: N

- PMC Wake Registers
- SCR Protection: WAKE_SCR_COAL_SCR_0
- Reset: 0x00000000 (0b0000,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000)
- Bit
- Reset
- Description
31:0 0x0 TIMER: wake coalescing timer for group0(shorter window) In order to be aligned, the value should be 1/N of AOWAKE_COAL_TIMER_GRP1
- WAKE_AOWAKE_COAL_GRP1_0
- Offset: 0x4e0
- Read/Write: R/W
- Parity Protection: N
- Shadow: N
- SCR Protection: WAKE_SCR_COAL_SCR_0
- Reset: 0x00000000 (0b0000,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000)
- Bit
- Reset
- Description
31:0 0x0 TIMER: wake coalescing timer for group1(longer window).
- WAKE_AOWAKE_TSC_CTRL_0
- One SCR for the following two registers
- Offset: 0x4e4
- Read/Write: R/W
- Parity Protection: N
- Shadow: N
- SCR Protection: WAKE_SCR_TSC_CNTRL_SCR_0
- Reset: 0x00000000 (0bxxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,x000,0000)
- Bit
- Reset
- Description
6:0 0x0 WAKE_INDEX: for TSC snapping shot, SW need to first program this register to indicate which wake event is selected to trigger the TSC snap.
- After programming this register, the TSC_SNAP_VALUE will be reset to 0,
and SW can continue to read TSC_SNAP_VALUE register, if the read back data is non-zero, it means that specific wake event has happened.
- WAKE_AOWAKE_TSC_SNAP_VALUE_0
- Offset: 0x4e8

- PMC Wake Registers
- Read/Write: RO
- Parity Protection: N
- Shadow: N
- SCR Protection: 0
- Reset: 0x00000000 (0b0000,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000)
- Bit
- Reset
- Description
31:0 0x0 DATA:
- Wake Time stamp value. Non zero value indiacates that wake event
has already happened. This value starts incrementing once the specific wake status gets updated
- WAKE_AOWAKE_DELAY_CELL_CTRL_0
- Offset: 0x4ec
- Read/Write: R/W
- Parity Protection: N
- Shadow: N
- SCR Protection: WAKE_SCR_GLB_CNTRL_SCR_0
- Reset: 0x00000022 (0bxxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xx10,0010)
- Bit
- Reset
- Description
5:0 0x22 SIG_DELAY_BUF_SEL:
- For glitch filtering, the requirement from various wakes is to filter
glitches on width ~2ns. This register needs to be configured to 0xE before delay filer is enabled.
- WAKE_AOWAKE_DET_EN_0
- One SCR for the following register
- Offset: 0x4f0
- Read/Write: R/W
- Parity Protection: N
- Shadow: N
- SCR Protection: WAKE_SCR_GLB_CNTRL_SCR_0
- Reset: 0x00000000 (0bxxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxx0)

- Scratch Registers
- Bit
- Reset
- Description
- FALSE
DET_ENABLE:
- This field is used to enable detection of wake inputs. This should be enabled
on SC7 entry after all other wake configuration steps are complete. SC7 HW sequencer also enables this bit befor VDD_RTC is powered off. In this case, all wake events that occured until that point are lost. Hence recommendation is for SW to explicitly set this bit on SC7 entry. 0 = FALSE 1 = TRUE
- WAKE_AOWAKE_CTRL_0
- Offset: 0x4f4
- Read/Write: R/W
- Parity Protection: N
- Shadow: N
- SCR Protection: WAKE_SCR_GLB_CNTRL_SCR_0
- Reset: 0x00000002 (0bxxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xx10)
- Bit
- Reset
- Description
- TRUE
GLOBAL_COAL_EN: 0: Disable Coal Across all wakes, 1: Individual Coal_en takes effect. This field is a bit to disable coalescing for all wake events at one shot. There is a mandatory requirement from HW angle to enable coelescing for all wake events. Hence this bit should never be set to 0. 0 = FALSE 1 = TRUE
- FALSE
INTR_POLARITY:
- INTR polarity, specified for PMIC interrupt
0 = FALSE 1 = TRUE
#### 4.2.4.3 Scratch Registers
- SCRATCH_SECURE_BL_SCRATCH_0
- Secure scratch for Boot Loader
Since scratch registers are moved to SRAM, the reset values proclaimed in the spec file do not hold good and that the registers need initialization. This is an array of 15 identical register entries; the register fields below apply to each entry. Full register list is: SCRATCH_SECURE_BL_SCRATCH_<i>, among which <i> belongs to <0..14>.
- Offset: 0x0,..,0x38

- Scratch Registers
- Read/Write: R/W
- Parity Protection: N
- Shadow: N
- SCR Protection: SCRATCH_SCR_BL_SCR_0
- Reset: 0x00000000 (0b0000,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000)
- Bit
- Reset
- Description
31:0 0x0
- DATA
